   29: =head1 NAME
   30: 
   31: App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor - Extract test schemas from Perl modules
   32: 
   33: =head1 VERSION
   34: 
   35: Version 0.31
   36: 
   37: =head1 SYNOPSIS
   38: 
   39: 	use App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor;
   40: 
   41: 	my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(
   42: 		input_file => 'lib/MyModule.pm',
   43: 		output_dir => 'schemas/',
   44: 		verbose	=> 1,
   45: 	);
   46: 
   47: 	my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all();
   48: 
   49: =head1 DESCRIPTION
   50: 
   51: App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor analyzes Perl modules and generates
   52: structured YAML schema files suitable for automated test generation by L<App::Test::Generator>.
   53: This module employs
   54: static analysis techniques to infer parameter types, constraints, and
   55: method behaviors directly from your source code.
   56: 
   57: =head2 Analysis Methods
   58: 
   59: The extractor combines multiple analysis approaches for a comprehensive schema generation:
   60: 
   61: =over 4
   62: 
   63: =item * B<POD Documentation Analysis>
   64: 
   65: Parses embedded documentation to extract:
   66:   - Parameter names, types, and descriptions from =head2 sections
   67:   - Method signatures with positional parameters
   68:   - Return value specifications from "Returns:" sections
   69:   - Constraints (ranges, patterns, required/optional status)
   70:   - Semantic type detection (email, URL, filename)
   71: 
   72: =item * B<Code Pattern Detection>
   73: 
   74: Analyzes source code using PPI to identify:
   75:   - Method signatures and parameter extraction patterns
   76:   - Type validation (ref(), isa(), blessed())
   77:   - Constraint patterns (length checks, numeric comparisons, regex matches)
   78:   - Return statement analysis and value type inference
   79:   - Object instantiation requirements and accessor methods
   80: 
   81: =item * B<Signature Analysis>
   82: 
   83: Examines method declarations for:
   84:   - Parameter names and positional information
   85:   - Instance vs. class method detection
   86:   - Method modifiers (Moose-style before/after/around)
   87:   - Various parameter declaration styles (shift, @_ assignment)
   88: 
   89: =item * B<Heuristic Inference>
   90: 
   91: Applies Perl-specific domain knowledge:
   92:   - Boolean return detection from method names (is_*, has_*, can_*)
   93:   - Common Perl idioms and coding patterns
   94:   - Context awareness (scalar vs list, wantarray usage)
   95:   - Object-oriented patterns (constructors, accessors, chaining)
   96: 
   97: =back
   98: 
   99: =head2 Generated Schema Structure
  100: 
  101: The extracted schemas follow this YAML structure:
  102: 
  103:     function: method_name
  104:     module: Package::Name
  105:     input:
  106:       param1:
  107:         type: string
  108:         min: 3
  109:         max: 50
  110:         optional: 0
  111:         position: 0
  112:       param2:
  113:         type: integer
  114:         min: 0
  115:         max: 100
  116:         optional: 1
  117:         position: 1
  118:     output:
  119:       type: boolean
  120:       value: 1
  121:     new: Package::Name # if object instantiation required
  122:     config:
  123:       test_empty: 1
  124:       test_nuls: 0
  125:       test_undef: 0
  126:       test_non_ascii: 0
  127: 
  128: =head2 Advanced Detection Capabilities
  129: 
  130: =over 4
  131: 
  132: =item * B<Accessor Method Detection>
  133: 
  134: Automatically identifies getter, setter, and combined accessor methods
  135: by analyzing common patterns like C<return $self-E<gt>{property}> and
  136: C<$self-E<gt>{property} = $value>.
  137: 
  138: =item * B<Boolean Return Inference>
  139: 
  140: Detects boolean-returning methods through multiple signals:
  141:   - Method name patterns (is_*, has_*, can_*)
  142:   - Return patterns (consistent 1/0 returns)
  143:   - POD descriptions ("returns true on success")
  144:   - Ternary operators with boolean results
  145: 
  146: =item * B<Context Awareness>
  147: 
  148: Identifies methods that use C<wantarray> and can return different
  149: values in scalar vs list context.
  150: 
  151: =item * B<Object Lifecycle Management>
  152: 
  153: Detects instance methods requiring object instantiation and
  154: automatically adds the C<new> field to schemas.
  155: 
  156: =item * B<Enhanced Object Detection>
  157: 
  158: The extractor includes sophisticated object detection capabilities that go beyond simple instance method identification:
  159: 
  160: =over 4
  161: 
  162: =item * B<Factory Method Recognition>
  163: 
  164: Automatically identifies methods that create and return object instances, such as methods named C<create_*>, C<make_*>, C<build_*>, or C<get_*>. Factory methods are correctly classified as class methods that don't require pre-existing objects for testing.
  165: 
  166: =item * B<Singleton Pattern Detection>
  167: 
  168: Recognizes singleton patterns through multiple signals: method names like C<instance> or C<get_instance>, static variables holding instance references, lazy initialization patterns (C<$instance ||= new()>), and consistent return of the same instance variable.
  169: 
  170: =item * B<Constructor Parameter Analysis>
  171: 
  172: Examines C<new> methods to determine required and optional parameters, validation requirements, and default values. This enables test generators to provide appropriate constructor arguments when object instantiation is needed.
  173: 
  174: =item * B<Inheritance Relationship Handling>
  175: 
  176: Detects parent classes through C<use parent>, C<use base>, and C<@ISA> declarations. Identifies when methods use C<SUPER::> calls and determines whether the current class or a parent class constructor should be used for object instantiation.
  177: 
  178: =item * B<External Object Dependency Detection>
  179: 
  180: Identifies when methods create or depend on objects from other classes, enabling proper test setup with mock objects or real dependencies.
  181: 
  182: =back
  183: 
  184: These enhancements ensure that generated test schemas accurately reflect the object-oriented structure of the code, leading to more meaningful and effective test generation.
  185: 
  186: =back
  187: 
  188: =head2 Confidence Scoring
  189: 
  190: Each generated schema includes detailed confidence assessments:
  191: 
  192: =over 4
  193: 
  194: =item * B<High Confidence>
  195: 
  196: Multiple independent analysis sources converge on consistent,
  197: well-constrained parameters with explicit validation logic and
  198: comprehensive documentation.
  199: 
  200: =item * B<Medium Confidence>
  201: 
  202: Reasonable evidence from code patterns or partial documentation,
  203: but may lack comprehensive constraints or have some ambiguities.
  204: 
  205: =item * B<Low Confidence>
  206: 
  207: Minimal evidence - primarily based on naming conventions,
  208: default assumptions, or single-source analysis.
  209: 
  210: =item * B<Very Low Confidence>
  211: 
  212: Barely any detectable signals - schema should be thoroughly
  213: reviewed before use in test generation.
  214: 
  215: =back
  216: 
  217: =head2 Use Cases
  218: 
  219: =over 4
  220: 
  221: =item * B<Automated Test Generation>
  222: 
  223: Generate comprehensive test suites with L<App::Test::Generator> using
  224: extracted schemas as input. The schemas provide the necessary structure
  225: for generating both positive and negative test cases.
  226: 
  227: =item * B<API Documentation Generation>
  228: 
  229: Supplement existing documentation with automatically inferred interface
  230: specifications, parameter requirements, and return types.
  231: 
  232: =item * B<Code Quality Assessment>
  233: 
  234: Identify methods with poor documentation, inconsistent parameter handling,
  235: or unclear interfaces that may benefit from refactoring.
  236: 
  237: =item * B<Refactoring Assistance>
  238: 
  239: Detect method dependencies, object instantiation requirements, and
  240: parameter usage patterns to inform refactoring decisions.
  241: 
  242: =item * B<Legacy Code Analysis>
  243: 
  244: Quickly understand the interface contracts of legacy Perl codebases
  245: without extensive manual code reading.
  246: 
  247: =back
  248: 
  249: =head2 Integration with Testing Ecosystem
  250: 
  251: The generated schemas are specifically designed to work with the
  252: L<App::Test::Generator> ecosystem:
  253: 
  254:     # Extract schemas from your module
  255:     my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(...);
  256:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all();
  257: 
  258:     # Use with test generator (typically as separate steps)
  259:     # fuzz-harness-generator -r schemas/method_name.yml
  260: 
  261: =head2 Limitations and Considerations
  262: 
  263: =over 4
  264: 
  265: =item * B<Dynamic Code Patterns>
  266: 
  267: Highly dynamic code (string evals, AUTOLOAD, symbolic references)
  268: may not be fully detected by static analysis.
  269: 
  270: =item * B<Complex Validation Logic>
  271: 
  272: Sophisticated validation involving multiple parameters or external
  273: dependencies may require manual schema refinement.
  274: 
  275: =item * B<Confidence Heuristics>
  276: 
  277: Confidence scores are based on heuristics and should be reviewed
  278: by developers familiar with the codebase.
  279: 
  280: =item * B<Perl Idiom Recognition>
  281: 
  282: Some Perl-specific idioms may require custom pattern recognition
  283: beyond the built-in detectors.
  284: 
  285: =item * B<Documentation Dependency>
  286: 
  287: Analysis quality improves significantly with comprehensive POD
  288: documentation following consistent patterns.
  289: 
  290: =back
  291: 
  292: =head2 Best Practices for Optimal Results
  293: 
  294: =over 4
  295: 
  296: =item * B<Comprehensive POD Documentation>
  297: 
  298: Write detailed POD with explicit parameter documentation using
  299: consistent patterns like C<$param - type (constraints), description>.
  300: 
  301: =item * B<Consistent Coding Patterns>
  302: 
  303: Use consistent parameter validation patterns and method signatures
  304: throughout your codebase.
  305: 
  306: =item * B<Schema Review Process>
  307: 
  308: Review and refine automatically generated schemas, particularly
  309: those with low confidence scores.
  310: 
  311: =item * B<Descriptive Naming>
  312: 
  313: Use descriptive method and parameter names that clearly indicate
  314: purpose and expected types.
  315: 
  316: =item * B<Progressive Enhancement>
  317: 
  318: Start with automatically generated schemas and progressively
  319: refine them based on test results and code understanding.
  320: 
  321: =back
  322: 
  323: The module is particularly valuable for large codebases where manual schema
  324: creation would be prohibitively time-consuming, and for maintaining test
  325: coverage as code evolves through continuous integration pipelines.
  326: 
  327: =head2 Advanced Type Detection
  328: 
  329: The schema extractor includes enhanced type detection capabilities that identify specialized Perl types beyond basic strings and integers.
  330: L<DateTime> and L<Time::Piece> objects are detected through isa() checks and method call patterns, while date strings (ISO 8601, YYYY-MM-DD) and UNIX timestamps are recognized through regex validation and numeric range checks.
  331: File handles and file paths are identified via I/O operations and file test operators, coderefs are detected through ref() checks and invocation patterns, and enum-like parameters are extracted from validation code including regex patterns (C</^(a|b|c)$/>), hash lookups, grep statements, and if/elsif chains.
  332: These detected types are preserved in the generated YAML schemas with appropriate semantic annotations, enabling test generators to create more accurate and meaningful test cases.
  333: 
  334: =head3 Example Advanced Type Schema
  335: 
  336: For a method like:
  337: 
  338:     sub process_event {
  339:         my ($self, $timestamp, $status, $callback) = @_;
  340:         croak unless $timestamp > 1000000000;
  341:         croak unless $status =~ /^(active|pending|complete)$/;
  342:         croak unless ref($callback) eq 'CODE';
  343:         $callback->($timestamp, $status);
  344:     }
  345: 
  346: The extractor generates:
  347: 
  348:     ---
  349:     function: process_event
  350:     module: MyModule
  351:     input:
  352:       timestamp:
  353:         type: integer
  354:         # min: 0
  355:         # max: 2147483647
  356:         position: 0
  357:         _note: Unix timestamp
  358: 	semantic: unix_timestamp
  359:       status:
  360:         type: string
  361:         enum:
  362:           - active
  363:           - pending
  364:           - complete
  365:         position: 1
  366:         _note: 'Must be one of: active, pending, complete'
  367:       callback:
  368:         type: coderef
  369:         position: 2
  370:         _note: 'CODE reference - provide sub { } in tests'
  371: 
  372: =head1 RELATIONSHIP DETECTION
  373: 
  374: The schema extractor detects relationships and dependencies between parameters,
  375: enabling more sophisticated validation and test generation.
  376: 
  377: =head2 Relationship Types
  378: 
  379: =over 4
  380: 
  381: =item * B<mutually_exclusive>
  382: 
  383: Parameters that cannot be used together.
  384: 
  385:     die if $file && $content;  # Can't specify both
  386: 
  387: Generated schema:
  388: 
  389:     relationships:
  390:       - type: mutually_exclusive
  391:         params: [file, content]
  392:         description: Cannot specify both file and content
  393: 
  394: =item * B<required_group>
  395: 
  396: At least one parameter from the group must be specified (OR logic).
  397: 
  398:     die unless $id || $name;  # Must provide one
  399: 
  400: Generated schema:
  401: 
  402:     relationships:
  403:       - type: required_group
  404:         params: [id, name]
  405:         logic: or
  406:         description: Must specify either id or name
  407: 
  408: =item * B<conditional_requirement>
  409: 
  410: If one parameter is specified, another becomes required (IF-THEN logic).
  411: 
  412:     die if $async && !$callback;  # async requires callback
  413: 
  414: Generated schema:
  415: 
  416:     relationships:
  417:       - type: conditional_requirement
  418:         if: async
  419:         then_required: callback
  420:         description: When async is specified, callback is required
  421: 
  422: =item * B<dependency>
  423: 
  424: One parameter depends on another being present.
  425: 
  426:     die "Port requires host" if $port && !$host;
  427: 
  428: Generated schema:
  429: 
  430:     relationships:
  431:       - type: dependency
  432:         param: port
  433:         requires: host
  434:         description: port requires host to be specified
  435: 
  436: =item * B<value_constraint>
  437: 
  438: Specific value requirements between parameters.
  439: 
  440:     die if $ssl && $port != 443;  # ssl requires port 443
  441: 
  442: Generated schema:
  443: 
  444:     relationships:
  445:       - type: value_constraint
  446:         if: ssl
  447:         then: port
  448:         operator: ==
  449:         value: 443
  450:         description: When ssl is specified, port must equal 443
  451: 
  452: =item * B<value_conditional>
  453: 
  454: Parameter required when another has a specific value.
  455: 
  456:     die if $mode eq 'secure' && !$key;
  457: 
  458: Generated schema:
  459: 
  460:     relationships:
  461:       - type: value_conditional
  462:         if: mode
  463:         equals: secure
  464:         then_required: key
  465:         description: When mode equals 'secure', key is required
  466: 
  467: =back
  468: 
  469: =head2 Default Value Extraction
  470: 
  471: The extractor comprehensively extracts default values from both code and POD documentation:
  472: 
  473: =head3 Code Pattern Recognition
  474: 
  475: Extracts defaults from multiple Perl idioms:
  476: 
  477: =over 4
  478: 
  479: =item * Logical OR operator: C<$param = $param || 'default'>
  480: 
  481: =item * Defined-or operator: C<$param //= 'default'>
  482: 
  483: =item * Ternary operator: C<$param = defined $param ? $param : 'default'>
  484: 
  485: =item * Unless conditional: C<$param = 'default' unless defined $param>
  486: 
  487: =item * Chained defaults: C<$param = $param || $self->{_default} || 'fallback'>
  488: 
  489: =item * Multi-line patterns: C<$param = {} unless $param>
  490: 
  491: =back
  492: 
  493: =head3 POD Pattern Recognition
  494: 
  495: Extracts defaults from documentation:
  496: 
  497: =over 4
  498: 
  499: =item * Standard format: C<Default: 'value'>
  500: 
  501: =item * Alternative format: C<Defaults to: 'value'>
  502: 
  503: =item * Inline format: C<Optional, default: 'value'>
  504: 
  505: =item * Parameter lists: C<$param - type, default 'value'>
  506: 
  507: =back
  508: 
  509: =head3 Value Processing
  510: 
  511: Properly handles:
  512: 
  513: =over 4
  514: 
  515: =item * String literals with quotes and escape sequences
  516: 
  517: =item * Numeric values (integers and floats)
  518: 
  519: =item * Boolean values (true/false converted to 1/0)
  520: 
  521: =item * Empty data structures ([] and {})
  522: 
  523: =item * Special values (undef, __PACKAGE__)
  524: 
  525: =item * Complex expressions (preserved as-is when unevaluatable)
  526: 
  527: =item * Quote operators (q{}, qq{}, qw{})
  528: 
  529: =back
  530: 
  531: =head3 Type Inference
  532: 
  533: When a parameter has a default value but no explicit type annotation,
  534: the type is automatically inferred from the default:
  535: 
  536:     $options = {}        # inferred as hashref
  537:     $items = []          # inferred as arrayref
  538:     $count = 42          # inferred as integer
  539:     $ratio = 3.14        # inferred as number
  540:     $enabled = 1         # inferred as boolean
  541: 
  542: =head2 Context-Aware Return Analysis
  543: 
  544: The extractor provides comprehensive analysis of method return behavior,
  545: including context sensitivity, error handling conventions, and method chaining patterns.
  546: 
  547: =head3 List vs Scalar Context Detection
  548: 
  549: Automatically detects methods that return different values based on calling context:
  550: 
  551:     sub get_items {
  552:         my $self = $_[0];
  553:         return wantarray ? @items : scalar(@items);
  554:     }
  555: 
  556: Detection captures:
  557: 
  558: =over 4
  559: 
  560: =item * C<_context_aware> flag - Method uses wantarray
  561: 
  562: =item * C<_list_context> - Type returned in list context (e.g., 'array')
  563: 
  564: =item * C<_scalar_context> - Type returned in scalar context (e.g., 'integer')
  565: 
  566: =back
  567: 
  568: Recognizes both ternary operator patterns and conditional return patterns.
  569: 
  570: =head3 Void Context Methods
  571: 
  572: Identifies methods that don't return meaningful values:
  573: 
  574: =over 4
  575: 
  576: =item * Setters (C<set_*> methods)
  577: 
  578: =item * Mutators (C<add_*, remove_*, delete_*, clear_*, reset_*, update_*>)
  579: 
  580: =item * Loggers (C<log, debug, warn, error, info>)
  581: 
  582: =item * Methods with only empty returns
  583: 
  584: =back
  585: 
  586: Example:
  587: 
  588:     sub set_name {
  589:         my ($self, $name) = @_;
  590:         $self->{name} = $name;
  591:         return;  # Void context
  592:     }
  593: 
  594: Sets C<_void_context> flag and C<type =E<gt> 'void'>.
  595: 
  596: =head3 Method Chaining Detection
  597: 
  598: Identifies chainable methods that return C<$self> for fluent interfaces:
  599: 
  600:     sub set_width {
  601:         my ($self, $width) = @_;
  602:         $self->{width} = $width;
  603:         return $self;  # Chainable
  604:     }
  605: 
  606: Detection provides:
  607: 
  608: =over 4
  609: 
  610: =item * C<_returns_self> - Returns invocant for chaining
  611: 
  612: =item * C<class> - The class name being returned
  613: 
  614: =back
  615: 
  616: Also detects chaining documentation in POD (keywords: "chainable", "fluent interface",
  617: "returns self", "method chaining").
  618: 
  619: =head3 Error Return Conventions
  620: 
  621: Analyzes how methods signal errors:
  622: 
  623: B<Pattern Detection:>
  624: 
  625: =over 4
  626: 
  627: =item * C<undef_on_error> - Explicit C<return undef if/unless condition>
  628: 
  629: =item * C<implicit_undef> - Bare C<return if/unless condition>
  630: 
  631: =item * C<empty_list> - C<return ()> for list context errors
  632: 
  633: =item * C<zero_on_error> - Returns 0/false for boolean error indication
  634: 
  635: =item * C<exception_handling> - Uses eval blocks with error checking
  636: 
  637: =back
  638: 
  639: B<Example Analysis:>
  640: 
  641:     sub fetch_user {
  642:         my ($self, $id) = @_;
  643: 
  644:         return undef unless $id;        # undef_on_error
  645:         return undef if $id < 0;        # undef_on_error
  646: 
  647:         return $self->{users}{$id};
  648:     }
  649: 
  650: Results in:
  651: 
  652:     _error_return: 'undef'
  653:     _success_failure_pattern: 1
  654:     _error_handling: {
  655:         undef_on_error: ['$id', '$id < 0']
  656:     }
  657: 
  658: B<Success/Failure Pattern:>
  659: 
  660: Methods that return different types for success vs. failure are flagged with
  661: C<_success_failure_pattern>. Common patterns:
  662: 
  663: =over 4
  664: 
  665: =item * Returns value on success, undef on failure
  666: 
  667: =item * Returns true on success, false on failure
  668: 
  669: =item * Returns data on success, empty list on failure
  670: 
  671: =back
  672: 
  673: =head3 Success Indicator Detection
  674: 
  675: Methods that always return true (typically for side effects):
  676: 
  677:     sub update_status {
  678:         my ($self, $status) = @_;
  679:         $self->{status} = $status;
  680:         return 1;  # Success indicator
  681:     }
  682: 
  683: Sets C<_success_indicator> flag when method consistently returns 1.
  684: 
  685: =head3 Schema Output
  686: 
  687: Enhanced return analysis adds these fields to method schemas:
  688: 
  689:     output:
  690:       type: boolean              # Inferred return type
  691:       _context_aware: 1           # Uses wantarray
  692:       _list_context:
  693:         type: array
  694:       _scalar_context:
  695:         type: integer
  696:       _returns_self: 1               # Returns $self
  697:       _void_context: 1            # No meaningful return
  698:       _success_indicator: 1       # Always returns true
  699:       _error_return: undef        # How errors are signaled
  700:       _success_failure_pattern: 1 # Mixed return types
  701:       _error_handling:            # Detailed error patterns
  702:         undef_on_error: [...]
  703:         exception_handling: 1
  704: 
  705: This comprehensive analysis enables:
  706: 
  707: =over 4
  708: 
  709: =item * Better test generation (testing both contexts, error paths)
  710: 
  711: =item * Documentation generation (clear error conventions)
  712: 
  713: =item * API design validation (consistent error handling)
  714: 
  715: =item * Contract specification (precise return behavior)
  716: 
  717: =back
  718: 
  719: =head2 Example
  720: 
  721: For a method like:
  722: 
  723:     sub connect {
  724:         my ($self, $host, $port, $ssl, $file, $content) = @_;
  725: 
  726:         die if $file && $content;                    # mutually exclusive
  727:         die unless $host || $file;                   # required group
  728:         die "Port requires host" if $port && !$host; # dependency
  729:         die if $ssl && $port != 443;                 # value constraint
  730: 
  731:         # ... connection logic
  732:     }
  733: 
  734: The extractor generates:
  735: 
  736:     relationships:
  737:       - type: mutually_exclusive
  738:         params: [file, content]
  739:         description: Cannot specify both file and content
  740:       - type: required_group
  741:         params: [host, file]
  742:         logic: or
  743:         description: Must specify either host or file
  744:       - type: dependency
  745:         param: port
  746:         requires: host
  747:         description: port requires host to be specified
  748:       - type: value_constraint
  749:         if: ssl
  750:         then: port
  751:         operator: ==
  752:         value: 443
  753:         description: When ssl is specified, port must equal 443
  754: 
  755: =head1 MODERN PERL FEATURES
  756: 
  757: This module adds support for:
  758: 
  759: =head2 Subroutine Signatures (Perl 5.20+)
  760: 
  761:     sub connect($host, $port = 3306, %options) {
  762:         ...
  763:     }
  764: 
  765: Extracts: required params, optional params with defaults, slurpy params
  766: 
  767: =head2 Type Constraints (Perl 5.36+)
  768: 
  769:     sub calculate($x :Int, $y :Num) {
  770:         ...
  771:     }
  772: 
  773: Recognizes: Int, Num, Str, Bool, ArrayRef, HashRef, custom classes
  774: 
  775: =head3 Subroutine Attributes
  776: 
  777:     sub get_value :lvalue :Returns(Int) {
  778:         ...
  779:     }
  780: 
  781: Detects: :lvalue, :method, :Returns(Type), custom attributes
  782: 
  783: =head2 Postfix Dereferencing (Perl 5.20+)
  784: 
  785:     my @array = $arrayref->@*;
  786:     my %hash = $hashref->%*;
  787:     my @slice = $arrayref->@[1,3,5];
  788: 
  789: Tracks usage of modern dereferencing syntax
  790: 
  791: =head2 Field Declarations (Perl 5.38+)
  792: 
  793:     field $host :param = 'localhost';
  794:     field $port :param(port_number) = 3306;
  795:     field $logger :param :isa(Log::Any);
  796: 
  797: Extracts fields and maps them to parameters
  798: 
  799: =head2 Modern Perl Features Support
  800: 
  801: The schema extractor supports modern Perl syntax introduced in versions 5.20, 5.36, and 5.38+.
  802: 
  803: =head3 Subroutine Signatures (Perl 5.20+)
  804: 
  805: Automatically extracts parameters from native Perl signatures:
  806: 
  807:     use feature 'signatures';
  808: 
  809:     sub connect($host, $port = 3306, $database = undef) {
  810:         ...
  811:     }
  812: 
  813: Extracted schema includes:
  814: 
  815: =over 4
  816: 
  817: =item * Parameter positions
  818: 
  819: =item * Optional vs required parameters
  820: 
  821: =item * Default values from signature
  822: 
  823: =item * Slurpy parameters (@array, %hash)
  824: 
  825: =back
  826: 
  827: B<Example:>
  828: 
  829:     # Signature with defaults
  830:     sub process($file, %options) { ... }
  831: 
  832:     # Extracts:
  833:     # $file: position 0, required
  834:     # %options: position 1, optional, slurpy hash
  835: 
  836: =head3 Type Constraints in Signatures (Perl 5.36+)
  837: 
  838: Recognizes type constraints in signature parameters:
  839: 
  840:     sub calculate($x :Int, $y :Num, $name :Str = "result") {
  841:         return $x + $y;
  842:     }
  843: 
  844: Supported constraint types:
  845: 
  846: =over 4
  847: 
  848: =item * C<:Int, :Integer> -> integer
  849: 
  850: =item * C<:Num, :Number> -> number
  851: 
  852: =item * C<:Str, :String> -> string
  853: 
  854: =item * C<:Bool, :Boolean> -> boolean
  855: 
  856: =item * C<:ArrayRef, :Array> -> arrayref
  857: 
  858: =item * C<:HashRef, :Hash> -> hashref
  859: 
  860: =item * C<:ClassName> -> object with isa constraint
  861: 
  862: =back
  863: 
  864: Type constraints are combined with defaults when both are present.
  865: 
  866: =head3 Subroutine Attributes
  867: 
  868: Extracts and documents subroutine attributes:
  869: 
  870:     sub get_value :lvalue {
  871:         my $self = shift;
  872:         return $self->{value};
  873:     }
  874: 
  875:     sub calculate :Returns(Int) :method {
  876:         my ($self, $x, $y) = @_;
  877:         return $x + $y;
  878:     }
  879: 
  880: Recognized attributes stored in C<_attributes> field:
  881: 
  882: =over 4
  883: 
  884: =item * C<:lvalue> - Method can be assigned to
  885: 
  886: =item * C<:method> - Explicitly marked as method
  887: 
  888: =item * C<:Returns(Type)> - Declares return type
  889: 
  890: =item * Custom attributes with values: C<:MyAttr(value)>
  891: 
  892: =back
  893: 
  894: =head3 Postfix Dereferencing (Perl 5.20+)
  895: 
  896: Detects usage of postfix dereferencing syntax:
  897: 
  898:     use feature 'postderef';
  899: 
  900:     sub process_array {
  901:         my ($self, $arrayref) = @_;
  902:         my @array = $arrayref->@*;        # Array dereference
  903:         my @slice = $arrayref->@[1,3,5];  # Array slice
  904:         return @array;
  905:     }
  906: 
  907:     sub process_hash {
  908:         my ($self, $hashref) = @_;
  909:         my %hash = $hashref->%*;          # Hash dereference
  910:         return keys %hash;
  911:     }
  912: 
  913: Tracked features stored in C<_modern_features>:
  914: 
  915: =over 4
  916: 
  917: =item * C<array_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>@*>
  918: 
  919: =item * C<hash_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>%*>
  920: 
  921: =item * C<scalar_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>$*>
  922: 
  923: =item * C<code_deref> - Uses C<-E<gt>&*>
  924: 
  925: =item * C<array_slice> - Uses C<-E<gt>@[...]>
  926: 
  927: =item * C<hash_slice> - Uses C<-E<gt>%{...}>
  928: 
  929: =back
  930: 
  931: =head3 Field Declarations (Perl 5.38+)
  932: 
  933: Extracts field declarations from class syntax and maps them to method parameters:
  934: 
  935:     use feature 'class';
  936: 
  937:     class DatabaseConnection {
  938:         field $host :param = 'localhost';
  939:         field $port :param = 3306;
  940:         field $username :param(user);
  941:         field $password :param;
  942:         field $logger :param :isa(Log::Any);
  943: 
  944:         method connect() {
  945:             # Fields available as instance variables
  946:         }
  947:     }
  948: 
  949: Field attributes:
  950: 
  951: =over 4
  952: 
  953: =item * C<:param> - Field is a constructor parameter (uses field name)
  954: 
  955: =item * C<:param(name)> - Field maps to parameter with different name
  956: 
  957: =item * C<:isa(Class)> - Type constraint for the field
  958: 
  959: =item * Default values in field declarations
  960: 
  961: =back
  962: 
  963: Extracted schema includes both field information in C<_fields> and merged parameter
  964: information in C<input>, allowing proper validation of class constructors.
  965: 
  966: =head3 Mixed Modern and Traditional Syntax
  967: 
  968: The extractor handles code that mixes modern and traditional syntax:
  969: 
  970:     sub modern($x, $y = 5) {
  971:         # Modern signature with default
  972:     }
  973: 
  974:     sub traditional {
  975:         my ($self, $x, $y) = @_;
  976:         $y //= 5;  # Traditional default in code
  977:         # Both extract same parameter information
  978:     }
  979: 
  980: Priority order for parameter information:
  981: 
  982: =over 4
  983: 
  984: =item 1. Signature declarations (highest priority)
  985: 
  986: =item 2. Field declarations (for class methods)
  987: 
  988: =item 3. POD documentation
  989: 
  990: =item 4. Code analysis (lowest priority)
  991: 
  992: =back
  993: 
  994: This ensures that explicit declarations in signatures take precedence over
  995: inferred information from code analysis.
  996: 
  997: =head3 Backwards Compatibility
  998: 
  999: All modern Perl feature detection is optional and automatic:
 1000: 
 1001: =over 4
 1002: 
 1003: =item * Traditional C<sub> declarations continue to work
 1004: 
 1005: =item * Code without modern features extracts parameters as before
 1006: 
 1007: =item * Modern features are additive - they enhance rather than replace existing extraction
 1008: 
 1009: =item * Schemas include C<_source> field indicating where parameter info came from
 1010: 
 1011: =back
 1012: 
 1013: =head2 _yamltest_hints
 1014: 
 1015: Each method schema returned by L</extract_all> now optionally includes a
 1016: C<_yamltest_hints> key, which provides guidance for automated test generation
 1017: based on the code analysis.
 1018: 
 1019: This is intended to help L<App::Test::Generator> create meaningful tests,
 1020: including boundary and invalid input cases, without manually specifying them.
 1021: 
 1022: The structure is a hashref with the following keys:
 1023: 
 1024: =over 4
 1025: 
 1026: =item * boundary_values
 1027: 
 1028: An arrayref of numeric values that represent boundaries detected from
 1029: comparisons in the code. These are derived from literals in statements
 1030: like C<$x < 0> or C<$y >= 255>. The generator can use these to create
 1031: boundary tests.
 1032: 
 1033: Example:
 1034: 
 1035:     _yamltest_hints:
 1036:       boundary_values: [0, 1, 100, 255]
 1037: 
 1038: =item * invalid_inputs
 1039: 
 1040: An arrayref of values that are likely to be rejected by the method,
 1041: based on checks like C<defined>, empty strings, or numeric validations.
 1042: 
 1043: Example:
 1044: 
 1045:     _yamltest_hints:
 1046:       invalid_inputs: [undef, '', -1]
 1047: 
 1048: =item * equivalence_classes
 1049: 
 1050: An arrayref intended to capture detected equivalence classes or patterns
 1051: among inputs. Currently this is empty by default, but future enhancements
 1052: may populate it based on detected input groupings.
 1053: 
 1054: Example:
 1055: 
 1056:     _yamltest_hints:
 1057:       equivalence_classes: []
 1058: 
 1059: =back
 1060: 
 1061: =head3 Usage
 1062: 
 1063: When calling C<extract_all>, each method schema will include
 1064: C<_yamltest_hints> if any hints were detected:
 1065: 
 1066:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all;
 1067:     my $hints  = $schemas->{example_method}->{_yamltest_hints};
 1068: 
 1069: You can then feed these hints into automated test generators to produce
 1070: negative tests, boundary tests, and parameter-specific test cases.
 1071: 
 1072: =head3 Notes
 1073: 
 1074: =over 4
 1075: 
 1076: =item * Hints are inferred heuristically from code and validation statements.
 1077: 
 1078: =item * Not all inputs are guaranteed to be detected; the feature is additive
 1079: and will never remove information from the schema.
 1080: 
 1081: =item * Currently, equivalence classes are not populated, but the field exists
 1082: for future extension.
 1083: 
 1084: =item * Boundary and invalid input hints are deduplicated to avoid repeated
 1085: test values.
 1086: 
 1087: =back
 1088: 
 1089: =head3 Examples
 1090: 
 1091: Given a method like:
 1092: 
 1093:     sub example {
 1094:         my ($x) = @_;
 1095:         die "negative" if $x < 0;
 1096:         return unless defined($x);
 1097:         return $x * 2;
 1098:     }
 1099: 
 1100: After running:
 1101: 
 1102:     my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(
 1103:         input_file => 'TestHints.pm',
 1104:         output_dir => '/tmp',
 1105:         quiet    => 1,
 1106:     );
 1107: 
 1108:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all;
 1109: 
 1110: The schema for the method "example" will include:
 1111: 
 1112:     $schemas->{example} = {
 1113:         function => 'example',
 1114:         _confidence => {
 1115:             input  => 'unknown',
 1116:             output => 'unknown',
 1117:         },
 1118:         input => {
 1119:             x => {
 1120:                 type     => 'scalar',
 1121:                 optional => 0,
 1122:             }
 1123:         },
 1124:         output => {
 1125:             type => 'scalar',
 1126:         },
 1127:         _yamltest_hints => {
 1128:             boundary_values => [0, 1],
 1129:             invalid_inputs  => [undef, -1],
 1130:             equivalence_classes => [],
 1131:         },
 1132:         _notes => '...',
 1133:         _analysis => {
 1134:             input_confidence  => 'low',
 1135:             output_confidence => 'unknown',
 1136:             confidence_factors => {
 1137:                 input  => {...},
 1138:                 output => {...},
 1139:             },
 1140:             overall_confidence => 'low',
 1141:         },
 1142:         _fields => {},
 1143:         _modern_features => {},
 1144:         _attributes => {},
 1145:     };
 1146: 
 1147: =head1 METHODS
 1148: 
 1149: =head2 new
 1150: 
 1151: Private methods are not included, unless C<include_private> is used in C<new()>.
 1152: 
 1153: The extractor supports several configuration parameters:
 1154: 
 1155:     my $extractor = App::Test::Generator::SchemaExtractor->new(
 1156:         input_file           => 'lib/MyModule.pm',  # Required
 1157:         output_dir           => 'schemas/',         # Optional - only needed if writing schemas
 1158:         verbose              => 1,                  # Default: 0
 1159:         include_private      => 1,                  # Default: 0
 1160:         max_parameters       => 50,                 # Default: 20
 1161:         confidence_threshold => 0.7,               # Default: 0.5
 1162:         strict_pod           => 0|1|2,              # Default: 0 (off)
 1163:     );
 1164: 
 1165: C<output_dir> is optional.
 1166: It is only required if schema files will be
 1167: written to disk. Callers that pass C<no_write =E<gt> 1> to C<extract_all>
 1168: do not need to supply it. If C<output_dir> is omitted and C<_write_schema>
 1169: is called, it will croak with a clear error message.
 1170: 
 1171: =cut

 1200: 
 1201: =head2 extract_all
 1202: 
 1203: Extract schemas for all methods in the module.
 1204: 
 1205: Returns a hashref of method_name => schema.
 1206: 
 1207:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all();
 1208: 
 1209:     # Suppress writing .yml files to disk (returns schemas only)
 1210:     my $schemas = $extractor->extract_all(no_write => 1);
 1211: 
 1212: Accepts an optional hashref or named parameters:
 1213: 
 1214: =over 4
 1215: 
 1216: =item * C<no_write>
 1217: 
 1218: When set to a true value, schema files are not written to C<output_dir>.
 1219: The schemas hashref is still fully populated and returned.
 1220: This is useful when the caller wants to inspect or augment schemas
 1221: before deciding whether and where to write them.
 1222: 
 1223: =back
 1224: 
 1225: The extraction process performs comprehensive validation of the agreement between
 1226: POD documentation and the actual code, controlled by the C<strict_pod> option
 1227: specified in the constructor. This validation operates at three distinct levels:
 1228: 
 1229: =over 4
 1230: 
 1231: =item * C<0> (default, no validation)
 1232: 
 1233: No POD/code validation is performed. Any disagreements between the documented
 1234: parameters in POD and the actual parameters in the code are silently ignored.
 1235: The extractor proceeds with schema generation regardless of inconsistencies.
 1236: 
 1237: =item * C<1> (warning mode)
 1238: 
 1239: Validation errors are collected and attached to each method's schema under the
 1240: C<_pod_validation_errors> key. The extraction continues even when errors are found,
 1241: allowing batch processing and comprehensive reporting. Errors include:
 1242:   - Parameters documented in POD but not found in code signatures
 1243:   - Parameters present in code but undocumented in POD
 1244:   - Type mismatches (incompatible types flagged as "Type mismatch")
 1245:   - Type differences (compatible but different types flagged as "Type difference")
 1246:   - Optional/required status disagreements
 1247:   - Constraint mismatches (min/max bounds, regex patterns)
 1248: 
 1249: =item * C<2> (strict mode)
 1250: 
 1251: The extraction immediately C<croak>s when the first validation error is encountered,
 1252: providing a detailed error message. This mode is useful for enforcing documentation
 1253: quality in development pipelines or CI/CD processes. Even compatible type differences
 1254: (such as POD "integer" vs. code "number") will trigger failure in this mode.
 1255: 
 1256: =back
 1257: 
 1258: Validation checks encompass parameter existence, type compatibility, optional/required
 1259: status, and constraint consistency. The system distinguishes between "compatible"
 1260: type differences (e.g., "integer" and "number", "array" and "arrayref") which are
 1261: tolerated in warning mode but still reported, and "incompatible" type mismatches
 1262: (e.g., "string" vs. "hashref") which are always flagged as errors. A comprehensive
 1263: validation report can be generated using the C<generate_pod_validation_report> method.
 1264: 
 1265: =head3 Pseudo Code
 1266: 
 1267:   FOREACH method
 1268:   DO
 1269:     analyze the method
 1270:     write a schema file for that method (unless no_write is set)
 1271:   END
 1272: 
 1273: =cut
 1274:

 5660: =head2 _analyze_relationships
 5661: 
 5662: Analyze relationships and dependencies between parameters.
 5663: 
 5664: Detects:
 5665: - Mutually exclusive parameters (can't use both)

 5667: - Conditional requirements (if X then Y)

 5669: - Value-based constraints (X=5 requires Y)
 5670: 
 5671: =cut

 6413: =head2 _needs_object_instantiation
 6414: 
 6415: Enhanced object detection that:
 6416: - Detects factory methods that return instances
 6417: - Recognizes singleton patterns
 6418: - Identifies when constructor needs specific parameters
 6419: - Handles inheritance (when parent class new() is needed)
 6420: - Detects both instance methods and class methods that require objects
 6421: 
 6422: Returns:
 6423: - undef if no object needed
 6424: - package name if object instantiation is needed
 6425: - hashref with constructor details if specific parameters are needed
 6426: 
 6427: =cut

 7067: =head2 _extract_default_value
 7068: 
 7069: Extract default values from common Perl patterns:
 7070: 
 7071: Patterns:
 7072:   - $param = $param || 'default_value'

 7075:   - $param = 'default' unless defined $param;

 7077:   - $param ||= 'default'
 7078: 
 7079: Returns the default value as a string if found, undef otherwise.
 7080: 
 7081: =cut
